  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer9203901342414976387">Peter is quick, daring, and full of mischief—and like all boys, he loves to play, though his games often end in blood. His eyes are sparkling gold, and when he graces you with his smile you are his friend for life, but his promised land is <i>not</i> Neverland.   <span id="freeText9203901342414976387" style="display:none">Peter is quick, daring, and full of mischief—and like all boys, he loves to play, though his games often end in blood. His eyes are sparkling gold, and when he graces you with his smile you are his friend for life, but his promised land is <i>not</i> Neverland. Fourteen-year-old Nick would have been murdered by the drug dealers preying on his family had Peter not saved him. Now the irresistibly charismatic wild boy wants Nick to follow him to a secret place of great adventure, where magic is alive and you never grow old. Even though he is wary of Peter's crazy talk of faeries and monsters, Nick agrees. After all, New York City is no longer safe for him, and what more could he possibly lose?<br /><br />There is <i>always</i> more to lose.<br /><br />Accompanying Peter to a gray and ravished island that was once a lush, enchanted paradise, Nick finds himself unwittingly recruited for a war that has raged for centuries—one where he must learn to fight or die among the "Devils," Peter's savage tribe of lost and stolen children.<br /><br />There, Peter's dark past is revealed: left to wolves as an infant, despised and hunted, Peter moves restlessly between the worlds of faerie and man. The Child Thief is a leader of bloodthirsty children, a brave friend, and a creature driven to do whatever he must to stop the "Flesh-eaters" and save the last, wild magic in this dying land.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9203901342414976387" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/476184-i-love-dark-retellings-but-the-ones-i">I love dark retellings, but the ones I read usually tend to be YA. Just how dark is this one?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_476184'><a id="like_count_community_question_476184" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/476184?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">2 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F6308379-the-child-thief">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/476184-i-love-dark-retellings-but-the-ones-i">5 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/476184-i-love-dark-retellings-but-the-ones-i">See all 4 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/7375157-karen"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1326079576i/7375157._UX100_CR0,16,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/7375157-karen">Karen</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Not as dark as I anticipated. I was hesitant to read it, but I love Peter Pan and Arthurian legend, so I went for it. Don't get me wrong, there was de<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Not as dark as I anticipated. I was hesitant to read it, but I love Peter Pan and Arthurian legend, so I went for it. Don't get me wrong, there was definitely some explicit gore and major moral ambiguity, and I certainly wouldn't let my 11 year old read it. Having said that, I thought it was fantastic and thought provoking. Not as gruesome or dark as say, George RR Martin's stuff. Plus, the illustrations are phenomenal and just add to the story. Definitely check those out prior to/while you're reading.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_791069960" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/791069960" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/791069960?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780061671340" href="/book/show/7802913-the-child-thief">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of DARK retellings</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2014">2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer791069960" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13823431080341284181"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>If the girl could only have spoken to the other boys and girls, the ones that had followed the golden-eyed boy before her, she would have known that there is always something left to lose.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/>This is a story you know - in a way. You remember how it goes, right? A boy called Peter appears to children and promises to take them to a better place, a place where they will never grow up and never get old. Of course we all know this story. But... what if it wasn't all that it seemed? What if Pe</span>
  <span id="freeText13823431080341284181" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>If the girl could only have spoken to the other boys and girls, the ones that had followed the golden-eyed boy before her, she would have known that there is always something left to lose.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>This is a story you know - in a way. You remember how it goes, right? A boy called Peter appears to children and promises to take them to a better place, a place where they will never grow up and never get old. Of course we all know this story. But... what if it wasn't all that it seemed? What if Peter held back dark secrets about the place he takes the children? What if there was a more sinister reason those children never got to grow up?<br><br>What I find most surprising is that I never realised how creepy and frightening the basic premise of <i>Peter Pan</i> could be when twisted ever so slightly. Think about it. A mysterious boy of unknown origin creeps through the windows of children's bedrooms and lures them away in the middle of the night. <u>Why was I never completely freaked out by this?</u> Well, now I'm terrified.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1401926831i/9869586._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>The Child Thief</i> is a lengthy, complex, but extremely compelling fantasy that weaves in elements of multiple folklore retellings, Arthurian mythology, historical fact and gorgeously creepy artwork. It should not be mistaken for a young adult novel, it's extremely graphic and disturbing in parts, but beautifully written and tinged with that inescapable sadness reminiscent of the original <i>Peter Pan</i> stories. It's at once a bloody horror story and a lesson in growing up - even the eponymous protagonist of the novel is simultaneously horrifying and endearing. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>We are the lost, the wild, the untamable.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>In this story, Peter seduces the children who are lost, abused and forgotten - the ones who have nothing left to lose and gladly follow the golden-eyed boy who makes enticing promises. At its core, this is a heartbreaking tale about the abandoned and unloved, and those who don't realise they're loved until it's too late. There are a lot of lessons floating around in this novel, plenty of philosophical musings on life and death. Those who believe this is vastly different from the original <i>Peter Pan</i> have clearly forgotten the darkness of Barrie's stories before the sugar-coated Disney version. I always remember the haunting line Peter says: <i>
  <b>"To die will be an awfully big adventure."</b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1401929299i/9870101.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It is a wonderful retelling for old fans, but it also stands on its own as an intricately-woven fantasy world full of wonder and danger. The characters face multiple threats from faeries, witches, pixies, flesh eaters and - perhaps the most bloodthirsty creatures of all - humans. The ending was sad in the perfect kind of way. I love that Brom has managed to create a main character that is some parts monster and some parts hero, you will probably find yourself wondering at times which he is and deciding that he is in many ways both. <br><br>Given the powerful effect this novel had on me and the way that it is completely unlike anything I've ever read before, how could I not give it five stars?<br><br><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://mycountryheart.co.uk/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCcVsMUSAzMlIKs3nw-xe_nw" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13823431080341284181" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_241779468" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/241779468" />
    <a title="Stephen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen"><img alt="Stephen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311616811p2/1413439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/241779468?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephen" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen">Stephen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780061671340" href="/book/show/7802913-the-child-thief">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=6-star-books">6-star-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=retellings-reimaginings-and-mashes">retellings-reimaginings-and-mashes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=dark-and-gritty">dark-and-gritty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=mythstories-and-legends">mythstories-and-legends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=children-behaving-badly">children-behaving-badly</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=2006-2010">2006-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer241779468" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14916930648681645542"><a href='http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Book%20covers/?action=view&current=102089103-1-1.jpg' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380364119i/715662.jpg' alt='Photobucket' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>This is a <b>MUST...READ...ALERT</b> fellow <i>Goodreaders</i>. Not only is this a <b>gorgeously</b> imagined and <b>supertastically</b> crafted retelling/reimagining/expansion of <b>Peter Pan</b>, but it's also <b>hands down, down, down</b> the <u>BEST</u> version I have ever experienced…which, no offense to James Barrie, includes the original.<br/><br/>This is a fantasy <b>master-piece</b> and has earned a prominent place on my list of all time favorite novels. This is not to be missed. <br/><br/>Before I stumble further into the <b>puddle of gush</b> I’m dripping, you s</span>
  <span id="freeText14916930648681645542" style="display:none"><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Book%20covers/?action=view&amp;current=102089103-1-1.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380364119i/715662.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This is a <b>MUST...READ...ALERT</b> fellow <i>Goodreaders</i>. Not only is this a <b>gorgeously</b> imagined and <b>supertastically</b> crafted retelling/reimagining/expansion of <b>Peter Pan</b>, but it's also <b>hands down, down, down</b> the <u>BEST</u> version I have ever experienced…which, no offense to James Barrie, includes the original.<br><br>This is a fantasy <b>master-piece</b> and has earned a prominent place on my list of all time favorite novels. This is not to be missed. <br><br>Before I stumble further into the <b>puddle of gush</b> I’m dripping, you should know that this tale is extremely <b>dark</b>, and I mean dark like black ink, and much of the narrative is steeped in pain, sadness, anger and loss that can suck the mood right out of you. I don’t think anything I say could do a better job of highlighting this point than the opening of the novel itself, which begins as follows: <blockquote>
  <i>It would happen again tonight: the really bad thing. The girl had no doubt. It had started a few months ago, around the time her breasts had begun to develop, and now, with her mother gone, there was no one to stop him.<br>From her bedroom she could hear him…He was in one of his fits, muttering to himself, cursing the television, his boss, Jesus, but mostly cursing her mother for taking all those pills...There came the sharp snap of a beer tab, then another, and another. Her hands began to tremble and she clutched them to her chest. She wished she could fall asleep…but she knew there’d be no sleep for her tonight. </i>
</blockquote> ...After a few pages of tension, darkness and [censored] followed, the prologue ends with the arrival of the titular character and the following ominous passage: <blockquote>
  <i>The boy came and knelt beside her. While she cried into her hands, he told her of an enchanted island where no grown-ups were allowed. Where there were other kids like her, who loved to laugh and play. Where there were great adventures to be had…What else did she have to lose?…If the girl could only have spoken to the other boys and girls, the ones that had followed the golden-eyes boy before her, she would have known that there is always something left to lose. </i>
</blockquote> How’s that for an <b>emotional wedgie</b> to open things up? Reading the opening prologue was like a shot in the gut and I think Brom handled it perfectly. He let the reader know immediately that this was not the Peter Pan from the Disney stories and they were preparing to embark on a journey that was dark and dangerous and different from what they have experienced before. <br><br>In the Afterward for this book, Brom mentions a line from James Barrie’s original story that you don’t find in the watered down version. It goes: “The boys on the island vary, of course, in numbers, according as they get killed and so on; and when they seem to be growing up, which is against the rules, <b>Peter thins them out</b>”. According to Brom, that one sentence and the suggestion that Peter actually kills the children that he takes forever changed Brom’s perception of Peter Pan as a innocent. From that single, brutal image, this version was born.<br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Book%20covers/?action=view&amp;current=Peter1-1.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380364119i/715663.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>However, even those that have read the original Barrie stories, the ones not watered down by convention and propriety, will find a much different Peter here. Every shred of the game-playing trickster has been transformed into a wounded, traumatized solider child whose pain has hardened him into a borderline sociopath. In his recruitment of children, he gives no thought to preying on their weaknesses in order to win them to his cause.<br><br>I thought it was fascinating and I was mesmerized from the very first page until the very last words…which are perfect, but I won’t spoil them. <br><br>BUT WAIT, THERE’S MORE…<br><br>However, this story is so, <b>SO</b> much more than just a retelling of Peter Pan. Brom tells the story of Peter Pan’s birth and the horrendous early years that shaped him into the legendary figure that his becomes. By doing so, he humanizes all that Peter does and it adds a depth to his character that no other adaptation has ever come close to equaling. As a character, Peter is amazing and I can not adequately express the praise Brom should receive for taking such a well known figure and completely fleshing him out. <br><br>BUT WAIT THERE’S STILL MORE…<br><br>In addition, Brom deftly combines the story with elements of English and Celtic myth and the Arthurian legend and weaves these threads seamlessly into the story. Neverland is recast as Avalon, the home of the faery folk ruled over by The Horned King and The Lady of the Lake. <br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Book%20covers/?action=view&amp;current=ladyweb1-1.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380364119i/715664.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>By incorporating this mythology, Brom transforms the central conflict of the story into a larger tale of humanity’s science and religion against the ancient world of faery. <blockquote>
  <i>Men-kind shared this world for but a blink, then, sadly, they became enlightened, found science and religion. The new world of men left little room for magic or the magical creatures of old. Earth’s first children were driven into the shadows by flame and cold iron, by man’s insatiable need of conquest.</i>
</blockquote> There are so many nooks and crannies to this world to explore that my head feels like it is going to burst trying to distill it down in this review. Let me just say that this is an epic story with a large cast painted against a wonderfully crafted setting that is perfectly realized by Brom.<br><br>WAIT, THERE’S STILL MORE…<br><br>Before I finish this <s>review</s> love letter to Brom, I want to make special mention of the characters. Richly drawn and well rounded does not begin to cover it. The characters in this story feel real and genuine. As such, they don’t always do what we want them to, but we always understand at some level, why they do it. None of Brom’s characters are stupid. They don’t take a wrong turn just to help the narrative along. The conflicts and problems the characters face arise organically and feel like life. <br><br>WAIT, ONE MORE THING AND THAT’S IT…<br><br>One final thing that I need to mention because it shocked the hell out of me. You won’t understand this until you read the novel, but Leroy is the biggest asshole of the entire story. He is a central thorn in the side of main character, Nick. Leroy does some absolutely despicable things during the story. Yet, for all of that scumbaggery, when late in the book Leroy tells his back story to Nick…my eyes welled up with tears…Brom needs some serious kudos for that, although some of the credit for this needs to go the audio narrator who was trying for an Oscar with his reading. <br><br>Anyway, this is an amazing novel and on the short list of my favorites of all time. You should read it right away. <br><br>6.0 stars. HIGHEST POSSIBLE RECOMMENDATION!!<br><br>P.S. The audio narration by Kirby Heyborne was as good as it gets and I strongly recommend checking it out if you listen to audio books. <br><br>P.P.S. In all my slobbering praise, I didn't even mention the artwork (examples above) which was stellar. Just an added perk in already overflowing bag of awesome. <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="14916930648681645542" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_68655829" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/68655829" />
    <a title="Will Byrnes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1526851-will-byrnes"><img alt="Will Byrnes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1291462190p2/1526851.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/68655829?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Will Byrnes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Will Byrnes" href="/user/show/1526851-will-byrnes">Will Byrnes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526851-will-byrnes?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526851-will-byrnes?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer68655829&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer68655829" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4959476435517643279"><blockquote>
<b>Like so many before me, I am fascinated by the tale of Peter Pan, the romantic idea of an endless childhood amongst the magical playground of Neverland. But, like so many, my mind’s image of Peter Pan had always been that of an endearing, puckish prankster, the undue influence of too many Disney films and peanut-butter commercials. <br/>That is, until I read the original Peter Pan, not the watered-down version you’ll find in the children’s bookshops these days, but James Barrie’s original and politi</b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText4959476435517643279" style="display:none"><blockquote>
<b>Like so many before me, I am fascinated by the tale of Peter Pan, the romantic idea of an endless childhood amongst the magical playground of Neverland. But, like so many, my mind’s image of Peter Pan had always been that of an endearing, puckish prankster, the undue influence of too many Disney films and peanut-butter commercials. <br>That is, until I read the original Peter Pan, not the watered-down version you’ll find in the children’s bookshops these days, but James Barrie’s original and politically uncorrected version, and then I began to see the dark undertones and to appreciate just what a wonderfully bloodthirsty, dangerous, and at times cruel character Peter Pan truly is.</b> - from the author’s site</blockquote>This is not your father’s Peter Pan. Brom found some rather un-Disney-like mayhem tucked into this supposedly children’s novel. In <i>The Child Thief</i> he explores those darker regions. Mixing a stew of old-world mythologies, which he very nicely sources for us at the end of the book, Brom has created a very dark view of a childhood lost. What manner of creature is Peter? How did he become the way he is, violent, sociopathic, with some serious mother issues, yet supremely charismatic, deft, and fun? A history is offered. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380348981i/703082._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="xxx" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Peter</b> – from the author’s site <br><br>One thing making the book a fun read is that it is a sort of <i>Where’s Waldo</i> of literary and mythological references. One battle might have been taken from C.S. Lewis, replete with diverse species joining forces. Our Virgil into this inferno is Nick, a Brooklyn kid beset by drug dealers who have taken over his single-mother’s home. Peter, on an ongoing mission to recruit fresh blood for this tale’s version of Lost Boys (and Girls), The Devils, is ever on the lookout for kids with nowhere else to turn. He saves Nick from deadly peril and leads him through the Mist to Avalon, a decaying former paradise, resonant with the many such darkening worlds in children’s literature. <i>A Wrinkle in Time</i> pops to mind, <i>The NeverEnding Story</i>. The darkness here touches some contemporary issues, as the nasty flesh-eaters, degraded Puritans who were trapped in the Mist of Avalon centuries ago, have been dredging up oil from beneath the surface and using it to burn supposedly inflammable, sentient trees in an attempt to push back the magic folk and gain control of the place for their own, and in so doing obliterating the magic to be found in nature, as embodied by Peter and The Lady. Their evil leader is familiar, the completely irrational, sadistic Torquemada type. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433481362i/15101047._SY540_.jpg" width="209" height="xxx" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380348981i/703083._SY540_.jpg" width="189" height="xxx" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>The Captain and The Reverend</b> - from the author’s site<br><br>Characters are not all so simplistic as the evil preacher. A Captain of the flesh-eaters (the local magic folk are decidedly vegetarian) turns out to be more than he appears. Nick struggles with his attraction to Avalon and the uber-mother, Lady of the Mist, while struggling to come to terms with his actions back in the real world. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433481362i/15101048._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="xxx" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There is considerable violence in this story, a body count that would be right at home in any contemporary video game (and yes, there is frequent mention of gameboys) and a chilling numbness on the part of most of the characters to the carnage. Arms, legs, and heads are chopped with enough frequency to carpet what remains of Avalon. It is a very male story, sort of a <i>300</i> for the pre-and-early-adolescent set. Far too much rah-rah-let’s-go-kill-some-flesh-eaters sort of speechifying. Can we zip up now and move along with the story?<br><br>There is a climactic big battle that I found a bit too much, even for this. But that is a quibble. Brom has wrought an interesting look at a classic character who has not seen much treatment of this sort before. Root questions are asked, and possible answers offered. <br><br>In addition, Brom has created beautiful black-and-white illustrations for the beginning of each chapter, and a set of full color paintings for the principal characters. <br><br><br>=============================<b>EXTRA STUFF<br><br>Links to the author’s <a href="http://www.bromart.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">personal</a>, <a target="_blank">Twitter</a> and <a href="https://www.facebook.com/Brom.Artist" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">FB</a> pages</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="4959476435517643279" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review68655829">

<div id="review_330033933" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/330033933" />
    <a title="Kat (Lost in Neverland)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5749698-kat-lost-in-neverland"><img alt="Kat (Lost in Neverland)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417030210p2/5749698.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/330033933?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat (Lost in Neverland)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat (Lost in Neverland)" href="/user/show/5749698-kat-lost-in-neverland">Kat (Lost in Neverland)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People who are not affected by heavy gore and swearing</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5749698-kat-lost-in-neverland?shelf=wtf">wtf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5749698-kat-lost-in-neverland?shelf=bloody-brilliant">bloody-brilliant</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5749698-kat-lost-in-neverland?shelf=depressing">depressing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5749698-kat-lost-in-neverland?shelf=blew-me-away">blew-me-away</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer330033933" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16986703077275005698">When you think of Peter Pan, you think of;<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380377817ra/733187.gif' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Or maybe;<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380377817ra/733188.gif' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The Child Thief has none of that. None at all. <br/><br/><br/>Upon finishing The Child Thief, I had an overwhelming urge, as if by magic, to go outside and <i>play.</i><br/><br/>So outside I ran, no shoes, completely barefoot, ran around in the grass, jumped high on the trampoline, feeling invigorated. My hair flew like it had a mind of its own, I could feel my hands and feet getting dirtier by the second; but I didn't care. Out of breath, I collapsed onto the trampoline, hair</span>
  <span id="freeText16986703077275005698" style="display:none">When you think of Peter Pan, you think of;<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380377817ra/733187.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Or maybe;<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380377817ra/733188.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The Child Thief has none of that. None at all. <br><br><br>Upon finishing The Child Thief, I had an overwhelming urge, as if by magic, to go outside and <i>play.</i><br><br>So outside I ran, no shoes, completely barefoot, ran around in the grass, jumped high on the trampoline, feeling invigorated. My hair flew like it had a mind of its own, I could feel my hands and feet getting dirtier by the second; but I didn't care. Out of breath, I collapsed onto the trampoline, hair splayed around my head, and gazed into the overcast sky, tiny droplets of rain coming down. And I thought.<br>I imagined myself as a Lost Child, running with Peter in Avalon, bloodlust in my veins, a knife in my hand, a grin on my face. I leaped out of trees to attack the evil Flesh-Eaters and howled like the demon I was, hungry for blood to be spilled and metal to meet flesh. Peter grinned at me, and I grinned back, for Peter's smile is the most contagious thing. <br><br><br>Sadly, we must all return to the world of reality, in a world of normal people with normal lives. People who don't see the magic around them, in the air in even the most darkest and most horrible of places. But Peter does. The Lost Children do. They always will. <br>Take it from Peter; who grew up feeling unloved and abandoned. Who stole children and taught them to kill, to crave blood and murder. He lives in a world of monsters and grey, yet still has magic in him...especially when he's slashing people's head off. <br>But don't, in any way, think this book is about magic. It's a different kind of magic; a freaky and possessed twin of magic that shows the cruelty of humans and the utter hypocrisy of Christians and God.<br>Now when I think back, The Lady was almost like God, in the way she seduced Peter with her words and made him think nothing other than her. That so many will die for her, for The Lady, and risk their lives saving her and doing her biding. <br><br>Poetic in so many ways, Brom brings together a twisted and insane version of <i>Peter Pan</i>, with blood and gore and swearing and death. Lots of death. <br>The bitter truth behind (Let me rephrase that, it was more like; <i>look at that, it's right in front of your face!</i>) his words are blunt and honest, his characters are amazingly complex and diverse, and makes me want to follow Peter into the Mist, forever his as a Devil...<br><br><br><br><br><br>I ran with Peter today....and I <i>played.</i> <br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="16986703077275005698" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1839618935" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1839618935" />
    <a title="Lyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn"><img alt="Lyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495541962p2/5253785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1839618935?book_show_action=true">Dec 26, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyn" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn">Lyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1839618935" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14146551646221497418">Very, very good.<br/><br/>The postmodern Peter Pan; more Pan than Peter.<br/><br/>Brom’s 2009 retelling of Peter Pan was enthralling. From the first few pages describing the mean streets of New York City and some excruciatingly graphic scenes of drug dealing cruelty and violence, the reader is held, shocked and awed, by his weird and unforgiving vision of J.M. Barrie’s characters told from the vantage of the 21st century.<br/><br/>Brom’s dark prophecy is as much Jack Vance and Michael Moorcock as it is early 1900s prose, wit</span>
  <span id="freeText14146551646221497418" style="display:none">Very, very good.<br><br>The postmodern Peter Pan; more Pan than Peter.<br><br>Brom’s 2009 retelling of Peter Pan was enthralling. From the first few pages describing the mean streets of New York City and some excruciatingly graphic scenes of drug dealing cruelty and violence, the reader is held, shocked and awed, by his weird and unforgiving vision of J.M. Barrie’s characters told from the vantage of the 21st century.<br><br>Brom’s dark prophecy is as much Jack Vance and Michael Moorcock as it is early 1900s prose, with a modern gamer perspective on rated M for mature violence, enough to make Anthony Burgess start gibbering in Nadsat. In an afterward by the author, as I was decompressing from the onslaught of HAVEATYOU!! Brom threw my way, he explained that he was actually inspired more by Barrie’s original story, which was far, far darker than anything Disney or Hollywood has tried to sell us over the years. <br><br>And his explanation is so on the money that he made me rethink my ideas of Disney’s Pan. Here is a fairy trickster god who kidnaps children from this world, takes them to another dimension where dismemberment and torture are par for the course, and places them in such insurmountable danger that he is required to again and again, for centuries, replace his ever-dwindling stock of lost boys. Think about it and Brom is right – if this were a happy frolicking Disney adventure, why does Peter need Wendy and her brothers? Where are all the previous lost boys? Where’d they go?<br><br>What makes this tribute to Peter Pan so mind bogglingly spicy to read is Brom’s portrayal of Captain Hook. Brom’s “The Captain” is not the insidious but charming villain portrayed by Disney, who sings ballads while playing a talented one-handed piano, this is a balanced and thoughtful leader of men who has been caught up in an ages long struggle between man and faery.<br><br>Blending elements of Gaimanesque mythology with traditional folklore and all under the rubric of an urban fantasy retooling of Peter Pan, writer and illustrator Brom has given us a dark but charismatic new world order for Neverland.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380404047i/786168._SY540_.jpg" width="218" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="14146551646221497418" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_72552154" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/72552154" />
    <a title="Dan Schwent" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent"><img alt="Dan Schwent" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593973948p2/870755.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/72552154?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dan Schwent" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dan Schwent" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent">Dan Schwent</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer72552154" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer260577003733885979">A runaway named Nick is fleeing the wrath of a drug dealer when he runs into an odd boy named Peter. Peter saves Nick and takes him to Avalon, recruiting him into gang of nearly feral boys called The Devils. With Nick's help, can the Devils overcome the Flesh Eaters, the transformed men who defile and destroy Avalon?<br/><br/>I picked this up because I'm interested in the unsanitized versions of familiar fairy tales. It turns out Brom is, too. Like a lot of people, I was familiar with Brom's art when I pi</span>
  <span id="freeText260577003733885979" style="display:none">A runaway named Nick is fleeing the wrath of a drug dealer when he runs into an odd boy named Peter. Peter saves Nick and takes him to Avalon, recruiting him into gang of nearly feral boys called The Devils. With Nick's help, can the Devils overcome the Flesh Eaters, the transformed men who defile and destroy Avalon?<br /><br />I picked this up because I'm interested in the unsanitized versions of familiar fairy tales. It turns out Brom is, too. Like a lot of people, I was familiar with Brom's art when I picked this up. It turns out he can write, too.<br /><br />The Child Thief is one hell of a grim retelling of Peter Pan. He's not prancing pixie in this, that's for sure. Peter is an amoral hero for the most part, as are the Sidhe, much more like Michael Moorcock's Melniboneans than Tolkien's elves. The Devils are more like the kids from Lord of the Flies than how the Lost Boys are normally depicted. For much of the book, two stories are told in parallel. One of Peter's birth and early days in Avalon, trying to fit in with Modron and the Sidhe, and one of Nick trying to fit in with the Devils.<br /><br />I didn't think the writing would be as good as it was since Brom is normally known as an artist. His prose is much better than I expected and the characters are well developed. I was particularly impressed with Peter and The Captain. You know the captain I mean...<br /><br />If you like your fantasy dark, this is your book. It should appeal to fans of Neil Gaiman and Tim Burton alike. Now go out and get it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="260577003733885979" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1304990823?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chantal " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chantal " href="/user/show/31668723-chantal">Chantal </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=best-reads-of-2015">best-reads-of-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=favourite-books">favourite-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=own-physical-copy">own-physical-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1304990823" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14724433165109038206"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"The darkness is calling. A little danger, a little risk. Feel your heart race. Listen to it. That’s the sound of being alive. It’s your time, Nick. Your one chance to have fun before it’s all stolen by them, the adults, with their cruelty and endless rules, their can’t-do-this, and can’t-do-that’s, their have-tos, and better-dos, their little boxes and cages all designed to break your spirit, to kill your magic".</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><b>Buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/32524334-nina' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nina</a> (Click for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1379204773' rel='nofollow noopener'>her review</a>).<br/><br/>I loved it. I loved it. I l</b></span>
  <span id="freeText14724433165109038206" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"The darkness is calling. A little danger, a little risk. Feel your heart race. Listen to it. That’s the sound of being alive. It’s your time, Nick. Your one chance to have fun before it’s all stolen by them, the adults, with their cruelty and endless rules, their can’t-do-this, and can’t-do-that’s, their have-tos, and better-dos, their little boxes and cages all designed to break your spirit, to kill your magic".</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><b>Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/32524334-nina" rel="nofollow noopener">Nina</a> (Click for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1379204773" rel="nofollow noopener">her review</a>).<br /><br />I loved it. I loved it. I loved it.</b> I seriously struggled writing this review because every time I think of this book I become a gushing, ineloquent mess. This book reminded me of what it means to be a total fangirl.<br /><br /><b>I know that no book is ever perfect. But in my opinion, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6308379.The_Child_Thief" title="The Child Thief by Brom" rel="nofollow noopener">The Child Thief</a> comes pretty close. Brom hasn’t just written a novel, he has created a masterpiece.</b> <br /><br />You know that feeling when you read a book and you feel like it was written just for you? Tailor-made? That was how I felt while reading this Peter Pan retelling.<br /><br />Why, you ask? Well, this book has…<br />-	An <b>antihero</b>. In case you don’t know, there is NOTHING I love quite as much as a realistic, consistent antihero.<br />-	A <b>kick-ass female character</b>. Brom’s version of Tiger Lily, loved her.<br />-	A <b>complex, well-developed fantasy world</b>. <br />-	An <b>infusion of all kinds of different mythology, folklore and fairy tales</b>. From Celtic mythology and Arthurian legend all the way to pagan myths. Is there anything better?<br />-	An <b>eclectic cast of characters who are flawed and complex</b>. All intriguing in their own right.<br /><br />But I’m getting ahead of myself. Let’s try to break this down (even though my words will never be able to make this book justice).<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34268.Peter_Pan" title="Peter Pan by J.M. Barrie" rel="nofollow noopener">Peter Pan</a> is one of my favorite classics and there is so much potential for Peter Pan retellings to be incredible because they offer so much room for originality, creativity and imagination. Still I was hesitant, having read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7514925.Tiger_Lily" title="Tiger Lily by Jodi Lynn Anderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Tiger Lily</a> earlier this year, I wasn’t sure if any retelling could ever compare. And really, the two don’t compare. They couldn’t be more different from one another. <br /><br /><b>This book is so strange and peculiar yet manages to instill in the reader a sense of <i>realism</i> that is awe-inspiring.</b> I believed <i>everything</i>. Nothing felt constructed or contrived, the whole story made so much sense once I could see the whole picture. The plot development felt organic. <b>It was tragic and heartbreaking but also filled with action and suspense.</b><br /><br />In this version of the Peter Pan story, Peter is portrayed as a seducer: he preys on the abused, mistreated, enslaved. He seeks out children who fit these categories – the children who themselves believe they have nothing left to lose – and essentially promises them a better life, a life in Avalon, a mysterious magical island where faeries and monsters are routine. Fourteen-year-old Nick is one of those boys and he follows Peter through the Mist. Nick quickly realizes however, that things aren’t the way he hoped them to be. <br /><br /><b><i>The Child Thief</i> is a very dark book.</b> From the first couple of sentences you can gather that this is not a book for children, or even a young adults. <b>It is often disturbing and violent, the writing is gory and the whole novel screams sadness, pain, fury, loss and guilt.</b> It contains many heavy issues such as child abuse, rape and torture and although it’s not about those things, they play a significant role in the story. Generally, I feel pretty neutral about books that are excessively gory and violent; it doesn’t bother me but I also won’t seek them out actively. More often than not, I found that authors use these descriptions to replace plot and worldbuilding, which makes me feel like they are only trying to appall or disgust me instead of telling me a story. This isn’t the case here: <b>Brom uses bloody and horrifying passages where they serve the story, where they enhance, where they add realism. Never did the descriptions overpower the plot.</b> <br /><br /><b>The writing itself is hauntingly beautiful.</b> Poetic where it needed to be, simple where it should have been. Easy to read yet reminiscent of the original Peter Pan. Perfectly suited to the story being told. <br /><br />Then there is the issue of pacing. <b><i>The Child Thief</i> is quite a lengthy novel and yet I wasn’t bored a single second. This book did not drag. Ever.</b> I was at the edge of my seat the entire time and sometimes I even had to put the book down because I was getting so excited I actually had trouble breathing, something that barely ever happens. After finishing it I felt drained and physically exhausted, as if I’d been the one to go through all these events.<br /><br /><b>The worldbuilding was amazing.</b> Avalon was a fascinating and well-constructed place but what I loved even more was the relation between Avalon and the “real” world. It was so interesting to see how the magic worked and how different people reacted to it; the internal logic was fantastic. <br /><br />Best of all were the characters. <b>Brom managed the elusive feat of creating a cast of characters that were simultaneously unlikable and endearing. There is no hero and no villain.</b> The characters are just people, real and genuine, and it worked perfectly. I loved almost all of them, and those I couldn’t love because they are just too despicable, I understood. <br /><br /><b>Peter himself was such a deliciously ambiguous character.</b> Part hero, part monster, he is self-centered and delusional, sadistic and foolhardy. In fact, he borders on being a sociopath; stealing away children for his own gain and satisfaction without thought to what is might do to them. He doesn’t hesitate to use their own weaknesses against them. <br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Everything comes with a price. Everything. Some things just cost more than others.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />And despite all his flaws, <b>I couldn’t help but love him</b>. Maybe it’s because I have a soft spot for antiheroes, but I found Peter to be an amazing character. The way Brom slowly presents his backstory to the reader greatly humanizes him and I felt so much empathy for this traumatized, lonely boy who was just trying to live the best life he knew how. A truly complex and layered character who will doubtlessly leave the reader intrigued. <br /><br />We also have <b>Nick</b>, the second main character besides Peter. <b>I was so fond of him.</b> I admit, when Nick was first introduced I was a little worried because I was scared he’d fall prey to special snowflake syndrome. BUT Brom completely turned it around, making Nick into an incredibly realistic character I could totally root for. His bravery was admirable. <br /><br /><b>All the Devils were great.</b> They were distinct and fleshed-out. None of them stupid; they made mistakes but not the kind that were just put in to help move the story along. These were real mistakes, understandable mistakes. It might be frustrating, but never annoying. <br /><br />There were characters like Leroy, Ulfger and the Reverend that I despised with a fiery passion and yet…I could understand where they were coming from. This book seriously messed with my mind and made me question everyone.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>When I come to rule I will put an end to their debauchery. Faerie shall become a force to be feared. Ulfger, a name spoken in frightful whispers. We will make men-kind remember their place and will hide behind the Lady’s Mist no longer.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />So much complexity.<br /><br />And then there are the <b>themes</b>. This book is just teeming with interesting philosophical questions about morality, life and death, and what it means to do the <i>right</i> thing. Brom comments on religious fanaticism and its consequences, colonialism, war and sacrifice. <b>If there was ever a book that perfectly portrays the meaning behind “there are two sides to every story” <i>The Child Thief</i> is it. <br /><blockquote><i><b>Both sides so blinded by their fear and hate of each other that they couldn't see they were all fighting for the same thing.</b></i></blockquote></b><br />It’s also a book about loneliness and what neglect can do us. I found it to be both extremely compelling and very meaningful. <br /><br />When I thought the book couldn’t get any better, there were sentences like this:<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>I’m…I am a god!</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Oh Brom, you were just trying to make my mouth water, weren’t you?<br /><br /><b>To sum up, I cannot praise this book highly enough.</b> For obvious reasons it isn’t a book for everyone, but if you can handle darker topics, I suggest you pick this one up. <b>A novel that is horrifying and enchanting, beautifully written and different from anything I’ve read. <br /><br />A serious contender for my favorite book of the year.</b><br /><br />P.S. I recommend getting the physical copy if you can. There are GORGEOUS illustrations by Brom himself that you don’t want to miss out on. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14724433165109038206" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1287964364" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner"><img alt="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532688964p2/31461418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1287964364?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=alternative-pov">alternative-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fave-ya-and-fantasy">fave-ya-and-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=unexpected-but-awesome">unexpected-but-awesome</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=knots-in-my-stomach">knots-in-my-stomach</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=retelling">retelling</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=2015-read">2015-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fairytales">fairytales</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1287964364" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer979966932198350404"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1432584842i/14984819._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This retelling brilliantly succeeds in going to the very core of what gives this heartbreaking feeling to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34268.Peter_Pan' title='Peter Pan by J.M. Barrie' rel='nofollow noopener'>Peter Pan</a> : <b>The raw loneliness of the Lost Boys</b>, and the ambiguity of Peter : a hero, you think? <i>Really?</i> <br/><br/>Well now. <b>There's no such thing as a hero in this book, and it was fantastic</b>. What is it with anti-heroes that captivates me so much? <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1432582329i/14984490._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>"The thief saw the fear, the confusion, and he smiled. <br/>What had led this child here : abuse, neglect, molestation? All of the above perhaps? It really d</b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText979966932198350404" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1432584842i/14984819._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This retelling brilliantly succeeds in going to the very core of what gives this heartbreaking feeling to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34268.Peter_Pan" title="Peter Pan by J.M. Barrie" rel="nofollow noopener">Peter Pan</a> : <b>The raw loneliness of the Lost Boys</b>, and the ambiguity of Peter : a hero, you think? <i>Really?</i> <br><br>Well now. <b>There's no such thing as a hero in this book, and it was fantastic</b>. What is it with anti-heroes that captivates me so much? <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1432582329i/14984490._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"The thief saw the fear, the confusion, and he smiled. <br>What had led this child here : abuse, neglect, molestation? All of the above perhaps? It really didn't matter to the thief."</b>
</blockquote><br>Indeed in my opinion - and I'm weighing my words here - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/172487.Brom" title="Brom" rel="nofollow noopener">Brom</a>'s Peter is the <u>most interesting</u> and above that, <i>realistic</i> Peter Pan whom I had the pleasure of meeting. <b>Selfish. Delusional. Reckless. Driven. Deadly. So, <i>so</i> lonely</b>. In a word, it seems impossible to describe him since his layers are so hard to unravel. Oh, man, how he is fleshed-out! <br><br>So, what did I think? <b>I thought he was <u>fascinating</u></b>, and despite his flaws, I couldn't bring myself to hate him, even if damn, how he's begging for it sometimes! I resented him, yes, but hated him? I couldn't. How to hate him when we know what he went through? How not to be moved by the heart-wrenching flashbacks in his childhood, full of betrayals and loneliness? When he's rejected on all sides? Actually I'm pretty sure that we're not meant to love Peter, who is lost in all his contradictions, who loves his island and his <i>Devils</i> fiercely but who doesn't hesitate to sacrifice them. Frankly, Peter shares many traits with sociopaths, as his aims justify any means in his head - <br><br>I cared about him anyway. Sue me. <br><br>And then, <b>there're the Lost Boys, some crazy, some brave, some cowards, all loyal to death to Peter. All of them... but Nick</b>. <br><br>Oh, <i>Nick</i>. How full of heartbreak his story is! He is the second main character besides Peter, and as it is, we get to follow his first weeks - months? - after Peter brought him in the Island. Nick isn't like the other Lost Boys. Nick doubts. Nick complains. Nick <i>questions</i>. Now, how could we not understand it? The guy's just been deceived into coming there under false pretends for crying out loud! <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"Ask them their story. Peter finds the lost, the left-behind, the abused. Is that not why you are here? Did Peter not save you?"<br>"Peter tricked me."</b>
</blockquote><br>As usual, a book which manages to make me care deeply about the characters is a win. These characters? They made my heartbeat increase, I was frightened, mad for them. I even cried, for Pete's sake! <b>In a word, they never, ever left me indifferent</b>. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1432582329i/14984491._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>"Men who fear demons see demons everywhere."</b>
</blockquote><br><b>Danger is everywhere in Avalon</b>. From the horrible creatures to the Witch and her cringe-worthy (but somehow hilarious) daughters, not to mention the sluaghs who took hold of the Mists, Peter and his <i>Devils</i> must always stay on the defensive, because every path can lead to death. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"It didn't make it okay. It didn't make the hurt any less painful later, but it got him through. And right now he just needed to get through. "</b>
</blockquote><br>God it was frightening at times - like, cringe-worthy frightening. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/172487.Brom" title="Brom" rel="nofollow noopener">Brom</a> succeeded in bringing to life so many magical beings from Scottish fairy stories and other folklores that I couldn't help but feel both horrified and enchanted. <br><br>Avalon is dying, suffering from the curse that the Flesh-eaters brought with them. Remember The Captain? Well, <b>don't expect pirates here, but bloodthirsty creatures whose goal is to chase all of the life out of the Island they call their home</b>. Or are they, really? Nothing is never as simple as it seems. <br><br>Avalon is dying, and Peter must save it. Will he be able to find allies in the Elves and other trolls who inhabit the island? How far will he go to fulfill what he considers as his mission? As I said, there's no hero here. No right choice. But war. War and its sacrifices. <br><br>Don't forget, though : <b>there's two sides to every story, and nothing is Manichean in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6308379.The_Child_Thief" title="The Child Thief by Brom" rel="nofollow noopener">The Child Thief</a></b>. NOTHING. <br><br>Of course I found this <i>wonderful</i>.<br><br>Let me tell you something : this book was dark, so dark. That's why it seems important to point that it is not a children book, far from it. Indeed we come across many disturbing scenes. <b>There is religious fanaticism. There is child abuse. There is violence. There is torture</b>. <i>I couldn't breathe</i>. <br><br>Once again, as painful as it was at times, the darkness oozing from the book offers us a more realistic tale in my opinion. Avalon isn't a place where we go to live adventures, <i>no</i>. Avalon is a place where we go when we're so hurting from our life that we can't make any other decision. Life is unfair, you know. And I hurt for them.<br><br>To sum up, <b>here's an outstanding dark retelling whose writing, beautiful and awe-inspiring, serves the story admirably</b>. Obviously I loved it - hence my 5 stars rating - but if I had to point something that could bother some readers, it would be <b>the pacing</b>. Indeed although I was never bored, I can't deny that I felt the need to stop several times. <i>Remember the feeling we get when we're forced to pause a book and that it loosens the tension?</i> Well, here, <u>it was the opposite</u>. I <i>needed</i> to stop to keep the tension alive, and wasn't able to read it in one sitting, or two, for that matter. <br><br>Now, if you're used to fantasy, or want to try it, <b>I'd say go for it, because in the end, following these characters is an incredible experience you won't soon forget</b>.<br><br>PS. Just look at the art - Isn't it wonderful? <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1432582329i/14984492._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1460244805i/18718125._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="979966932198350404" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1249014350" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1249014350" />
    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1249014350?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Stephen King and Lord of the Flies fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=he-s-so-bad-but-he-does-it-so-well">he-s-so-bad-but-he-does-it-so-well</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=pants-are-snowmen-and-they-are-june">pants-are-snowmen-and-they-are-june</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=bye-bye-nineteenth-amendment">bye-bye-nineteenth-amendment</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=fabulous-five-stars">fabulous-five-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=creepy-yet-entertaining">creepy-yet-entertaining</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1249014350" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13800589753229032806"><blockquote>
  <i>"In a small corner of Prospect Park, in the borough of Brooklyn, New York, a thief lay hidden in the trees. This thief wasn't searching for an unattended purse, cell phone, or camera. This thief was looking for a child."</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>THIS. This is how you start a book. This is how you grab my attention, keep me reading through lectures, ignore my duties, and instill a burning need to search up The Child Thief fanfiction ASAP. Because I <i>have</i> to know what happens next. And once writers grab you by the have-</span>
  <span id="freeText13800589753229032806" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"In a small corner of Prospect Park, in the borough of Brooklyn, New York, a thief lay hidden in the trees. This thief wasn't searching for an unattended purse, cell phone, or camera. This thief was looking for a child."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>THIS. This is how you start a book. This is how you grab my attention, keep me reading through lectures, ignore my duties, and instill a burning need to search up The Child Thief fanfiction ASAP. Because I <i>have</i> to know what happens next. And once writers grab you by the have-to, it's all over.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1428747571ra/14478145.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The Child Thief is a gothic retelling of Peter Pan that would bring <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3389.Stephen_King" title="Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Stephen King</a> to his knees. <br><br>You're used to cute little Disney Peter or the slightly hotter one from the live-action reboot. Once Upon A Time has a Peter Pan too, I hear. <i>This</i> Peter is nowhere near sweet.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"His eyes gleamed at the thought. Hell, and it'd be fun too. Watching their faces as they juggled their guts."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>He's an antihero of the likes of Tyrion Lannister. A changeling, he was abandoned by his mother and left to the wolves. Goll the cannibal raised him before he got slaughtered by grown-ups. So when he walks into a mysterious mist and emerges in a tropical wonderland, you can hardly blame him for wanting to stay.<br><br>But Avalon (Neverland) is dying. The Lady of the Lake, guardian of Avalon, is withering away. So what does our brave hero do? Kidnap some abused kids, ones who have nothing to stay on earth for anyway and train them to fight his war.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"It's at a secret place. An enchanted island. No grown-ups allowed. It's full of faeries, goblins and trolls. We can stay up as late as we want. No teachers or parents to tell us what to do. We don't have to take baths, brush our teeth or make our beds."</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1428747571ra/14478146.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Peter Pan reminds me of Puck from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6644117.The_Iron_King__The_Iron_Fey___1_" title="The Iron King (The Iron Fey, #1) by Julie Kagawa" rel="nofollow noopener">The Iron King</a>, but on steroids. Vicious, playful, and a streak of loyalty that stretches as far as his interests. <br><br><b>And I fucking love him.</b> I want to take him in my arms, give him a cookie, then do nasty, nasty things to him on my bed. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1417470722ra/12389595.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>My copy contains a mini-interview, where the author says his Peter Pan was, in fact, inspired by Robin Goodfellow, which in turn stems from pagan wilderness gods. Brom mixes fey folklore and pagan myths really well here and tosses a dash of horror in for kicks. Because Peter Pan, if you really think about it, is hella disturbing.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1428747571ra/14478147.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There's this other character Nick, who I pegged for a special snowflake at first since Peter noted his resolve in the Mist and said no kid had ever found him again after he strayed from the path.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Nick,” Peter said, his words quick and urgent. “No matter what you hear, no matter what you see, ignore them. Avoid their eyes. And whatever you do, don’t dare speak to them.” Peter glanced into the fog. “If you lose the path Nick, your bones will never leave the Mist.” </i>
</blockquote><br><br>He's brave, stout of heart and does handy stuff with a spear, blah, blah, blah. Plus, he got mad at his mom for not buying him expensive skater sneakers when she had to rent their house out to drug-dealers to make ends meet.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1428747571ra/14478148.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Then because Brom is awesome, Nick changes. He becomes a <b>well-rounded, complex character I could root for. </b><br><br>Honestly, I don't think there's a character I actually hate. Not Leroy the bully or the fanatic Reverend. The Captain <s>Hook</s> is supposed to be the enemy and man, my heart aches for him. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1428747571ra/14478149.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yup, that guy. He's not the fiendish, mustachioed man Disney makes him out to be. <b>He's a father to two boys and just wants to get home.</b> Them fighting to leave Avalon like Peter wants them to would almost be funny if it wasn't so tragic.<br><br>Slight sexism aside (there are few prominent female characters), The Child Thief is the most awesome thing I've read in a long time. Last time I gave a book five stars without hesitation was in 2014 for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18172465.A_World_Without_Princes__The_School_for_Good_and_Evil___2_" title="A World Without Princes (The School for Good and Evil, #2) by Soman Chainani" rel="nofollow noopener">A World Without Princes</a>. That should give you an idea of its brilliance.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13800589753229032806" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
